**Result:**

---  
name: recheck  
description: recheck the last committed changes  
model: sonnet  
---  

Use this skill to trigger a full automated code review of the latest committed changes.  

The pipeline uses 4 agents in a named worktree:  
- **RO** (rechecker-orchestrator): Opus orchestrator — runs all 4 loops, makes 1 commit  
- **OCR** (opus-code-reviewer): Opus swarm worker — finds correctness bugs  
- **OFR** (opus-functionality-reviewer): Opus swarm worker — checks intent vs reality  
- **SCF** (sonnet-code-fixer): Sonnet swarm worker — applies fixes  

**This skill runs synchronously.** You are responsible for merging the worktree branch, resolving any conflicts, copying the report, and cleaning up. Do NOT leave unmerged branches behind.  

## Naming convention  

All files use the prefix `rck-{YYYYMMDD_HHMMSS}_{UUID6}`:  
- Worktree name: `rck-20260321_193000_a1b2c3`  
- Branch: `worktree-rck-20260321_193000_a1b2c3`  
- Report: `rck-20260321_193000_a1b2c3-report.md`  

Generate the tag at the start and use it throughout:  
```bash
RCK_TAG="rck-$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)_$(head -c3 /dev/urandom | xxd -p | head -c6)"
```

## Checklist  

Copy and use this checklist to track progress:  

- [ ] **Pre-check: verify git repo**:  
  ```bash
  git rev-parse --show-toplevel
  ```
  If it fails, tell the user "Not in a git repository — rechecker requires git" and STOP.  
- [ ] **Generate the tag** and store it (you will use it in every subsequent step):  
  ```bash
  RCK_TAG="rck-$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)_$(head -c3 /dev/urandom | xxd -p | head -c6)"
  echo "$RCK_TAG"
  ```
- [ ] Identify the latest commit SHA and changed files:  
  ```bash
  cd "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)" && git log -1 --format=%H && git show --name-only --format= --diff-filter=d HEAD
  ```
- [ ] **Launch the orchestrator in a worktree** using the tag as the worktree name:  
  ```bash
  cd "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)" && claude --worktree "$RCK_TAG" \
    --agent "rechecker-plugin:rechecker-orchestrator" \
    --dangerously-skip-permissions \
    -

... [1161 more chars truncated]

**Summary of what was changed in `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-5ec6f8/services/plugin-builder-service.ts`:**  

1. Added `operationQueue` array and `acquireSlot()` function after the `MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS` / `activeOps` declarations. `acquireSlot()` atomically checks-and-increments `activeOps` (synchronous, no `await` between check and increment) and returns a `release` callback. If all slots are full it queues the caller and resolves when a slot is freed.  

2. In `buildPlugin`: replaced `activeOps++` / `activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)` with `const release = await acquireSlot()`, `.finally(release)` on the async `runBuild` chain, and `release()` in the setup-failure catch block.  

3. In `scanRepo`: same replacement — `const release = await acquireSlot()` before the try, `release()` in the finally.  

4. In `pushToGitHub`: same replacement — `const release = await acquireSlot()` before the try, `release()` in the finally.

    28→**Problem**: The `key` prop for the mapped skill `div` elements is set to `skill.path`. While `skill.path` might be unique within a single scan result, it's not guaranteed to be globally unique across different repository URLs or branches. If a user scans `repoA` and finds a skill at `path/to/skill`, then scans `repoB` which also has a skill at `path/to/skill`, React will reuse the component instance, leading to potential rendering issues, incorrect state, or unexpected behavior, especially if the `selectedSkillKeys` logic relies on a unique key.      1→/**  
     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/plugin-builder/push - Push manifest to user's fork  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     8→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig  
    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(  
    18→        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },  
    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json(  
    25→        { error: 'Manifest is required' },  
    26→        { status: 400 }  
    27→      )  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)  
    31→  
    32→    if (result.error) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json(  
    34→        { error: result.error },  
    35→        { status: result.status }  
    36→      )  
    37→    }  
    38→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    39→  } catch (error) {  
    40→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
    41→    return NextResponse.json(  
    42→      { error: 'Invalid request body' },  
    43→      { status: 400 }  
    44→    )  
    45→  }  
    46→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:46:40]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The findings are clear. There is one real bug to fix: at line 35, `result.status` is used directly without validating it is a valid HTTP error status code (400-599).     if (result.error) {
      // Guard: only use result.status if it is a valid HTTP error code (400-599),
      // otherwise default to 500 to avoid returning a non-error status with an error body.
      const statusCode =
        typeof result.status === 'number' &&
        result.status >= 400 &&
        result.status < 600
          ? result.status
          : 500
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: statusCode }
      )
    }

     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API

     4→ * POST /api/plugin-builder/push - Push manifest to user's fork  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     8→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig  
    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(  
    18→        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },  
    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json(  
    25→        { error: 'Manifest is required' },  
    26→        { status: 400 }  
    27→      )  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)  
    31→  
    32→    if (result.error) {  
    33→      // Guard: only use result.status if it is a valid HTTP error code (400-599),  
    34→      // otherwise default to 500 to avoid returning a non-error status with an error body.  
    35→      const statusCode =  
    36→        typeof result.status === 'number' &&  
    37→        result.status >= 400 &&  
    38→        result.status < 600  
    39→          ? result.status  
    40→          : 500  
    41→      return NextResponse.json(  
    42→        { error: result.error },  
    43→        { status: statusCode }  
    44→      )  
    45→    }  
    46→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    47→  } catch (error) {  
    48→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
    49→    return NextResponse.json(  
    50→      { error: 'Invalid request body' },  
    51→      { status: 400 }  
    52→    )  
    53→  }  
    54→}  
    55→  

[system reminder collapsed]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:52:29]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I have read the full file. The `pushing` state variable exists (line 27). The "Push to GitHub" button at line 190-197 is disabled with `!isComplete || building`, but it should be `!isComplete || pushing` — because while a push is in progress, the button that toggles the push panel should also be disabled to prevent re-triggering the push flow. The `building` condition is semantically incorrect here: building being true already means `isComplete` is false (no result yet), so `building` adds no protection. Meanwhile, if `pushing` is true, the button should be locked to prevent toggling the push panel open/closed mid-push.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:47:10]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the information needed. Let me compile the facts:  

**Synchronous functions** (return `ServiceResult<T>` directly, NOT a Promise — do NOT add `await`):  
- `getSystemConfig()` — sync  
- `getOrganization()` — sync  
- `setOrganizationName()` — sync  
- `getSubconsciousStatus()` (from `config-service`) — sync  
- `parseConversationFile()` — sync  
- `getExportJobStatus()` — sync  
- `deleteExportJob()` — sync  
- `broadcastActivityUpdate()` — sync  
- `getStartupInfo()` — sync  
- `registerAgent()` (from `agents-core-service`) — sync  
- `lookupAgentByName()` — sync  
- `getDirectory()` — sync  
- `lookupAgentByDirectoryName()` — sync  

So the review's "missing await" bugs are all false positives — these functions are all synchronous. The review was speculative ("if they were to become asynchronous"). Per my instructions: "Only add `await` where the called function actually returns a Promise (i.e., is truly async). Do NOT add `await` to synchronous functions."  

Now let me check the real bugs — the inconsistent error handling ones. Let me read the rest of the file to see all the affected routes.

Now I have a complete picture. Let me analyze the actual bugs to fix:  

**Bug 1 — `GET /api/sessions` and `GET /api/sessions/activity`**: These use `sendJson` directly in error paths instead of `sendServiceResult`. The success paths also bypass `sendServiceResult`. Since the service doesn't return `ServiceResult`, using `sendServiceResult(res, { status: 500, error: ... })` in the catch block is the right fix.

      const rawBody = await readRawBody(req)
      const { file, options: optionsStr } = parseMultipart(rawBody, contentType)

      if (!file) {
        sendJson(res, 400, { error: 'No file provided' })
        return
      }

      const options = optionsStr ? JSON.parse(optionsStr) : {}
      const result = await importAgent(file, options)
      sendServiceResult(res, result)
    } catch (error) {
      sendJson(res, 500, { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Unknown error' })
    }
  }},

**New:**

  // Agent import (multipart form-data)
  { method: 'POST', pattern: /^\/api\/agents\/import$/, paramNames: [], handler: async (req, res) => {
    try {
      const contentType = getHeader(req, 'content-type') || ''
      const rawBody = await readRawBody(req)
      const { file, options: optionsStr } = parseMultipart(rawBody, contentType)

      if (!file) {
        sendServiceResult(res, { status: 400, error: 'No file provided' })
        return
      }

      const options = optionsStr ? JSON.parse(optionsStr) : {}

   492→    return { error: `Failed to scan repository: ${message}`, status: 500 }  
   493→  } finally {  
   494→    release()  
   495→  }  
   496→}  
   497→  
   498→/**  
   499→ * Push a generated manifest to the user's fork on GitHub.  
   500→ */  
   501→export async function pushToGitHub(config: PluginPushConfig): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginPushResult>> {  
   502→  // Validate fork URL  
   503→  if (!config.forkUrl || typeof config.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
   504→    return { error: 'Fork URL is required', status: 400 }  
   505→  }  
   506→  const urlErr = validateGitUrl(config.forkUrl)  
   507→  if (urlErr) return { error: urlErr, status: 400 }  
   508→  
   509→  // Validate manifest  
   510→  if (!config.manifest || typeof config.manifest !== 'object') {  
   511→    return { error: 'Manifest is required', status: 400 }  
   512→  }  
   513→  
   514→  // Validate branch  
   515→  const branch = config.branch || 'main'  
   516→  const refErr = validateGitRef(branch)  
   517→  if (refErr) return { error: refErr, status: 400 }

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:46:59]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a complete picture of the bug. Let me analyze it precisely:  

**The race condition in `buildPlugin`:**  
- The check `if (activeOps >= MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS)` and `activeOps++` are not atomic (lines 315 and 323)  
- There is a `try/catch` where `activeOps++` happens inside `try` (line 323)  
- The `finally` for `activeOps` decrement is attached to `runBuild(...).catch(...).finally(...)` — an async chain that runs after the function already returned 202  
- The synchronous `catch` block at line 384 also decrements `activeOps` — but only for the case where setup fails BEFORE the async chain is launched  
- This means: if setup fails AFTER `activeOps++` but the catch at line 383 runs AND the `.finally()` at line 378 also runs, `activeOps` gets decremented twice (double-decrement)  

Wait — let me re-read this carefully. The `try` at line 319 wraps the entire setup including the `runBuild(...).finally(...)` chain start. The `catch` at line 383 catches synchronous errors from setup. The `.finally()` at line 378 runs after `runBuild` completes (asynchronously). These are mutually exclusive paths — if an error is thrown during setup (before `runBuild` is called), the `.finally()` on the promise chain won't run because `runBuild` was never called.  

But wait — if `activeOps++` (line 323) runs, and then something throws synchronously BEFORE the `runBuild(...).catch(...).finally(...)` call at line 367, both the `catch` block (line 383-387) which decrements `activeOps` AND then the `.finally` would NOT fire (since `runBuild` wasn't reached). That's actually fine — only one decrement.  

The actual race condition is: check on line 315 and increment on line 323 are not atomic. Two concurrent calls can both pass the check and both increment.  

The review's suggested fix (a queue mechanism) is the right approach. Now let me implement it correctly.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:47:05]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. Let me implement the fix.  

The core issue: the `if (activeOps >= MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS)` check and `activeOps++` are non-atomic in an async environment — multiple concurrent callers can all pass the check before any of them increments the counter, allowing more than `MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS` operations to run simultaneously.  

The fix: replace the bare counter + check pattern with a queue-based `runWithConcurrencyLimit` helper that atomically acquires a slot (check+increment happen synchronously before any `await`), queues excess requests, and drains the queue when a slot is released.  

**Step 1:** Replace the module-level `activeOps` variable with the queue infrastructure.  

</div>

/** Max concurrent build/scan operations */
const MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS = 3
let activeOps = 0
```

**New:**  
```
/** Max concurrent build/scan operations */
const MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS = 3
let activeOps = 0
const operationQueue: Array<() => void> = []

/**
 * Acquire a concurrency slot.
 * Returns a release function that MUST be called in a finally block.
 * If MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS slots are already taken, queues the caller and
 * resolves only when a slot becomes available — no busy-waiting, no race.
 *
 * The check-and-increment is synchronous (no await between them), so two
 * concurrent callers cannot both slip through the MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS guard.
 */
function acquireSlot(): Promise<() => void> {
  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {
    const tryAcquire = () => {
      // Synchronous check-and-increment: no await between them, so this is
      // the only place activeOps grows and it is always paired with a release.
      if (activeOps < MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS) {
        activeOps++
        resolve(() => {
          activeOps--
          // Wake the next queued operation, if any.
          if (operationQueue.length > 0) {
            const next = operationQueue.shift()!
            next()
          }
        })
      } else {
        operationQueue.push(tryAcquire)
      }
    }
    tryAcquire()
  })
}
```

**Result:**

**Result:**

    48→/** Max concurrent build/scan operations */  
    49→const MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS = 3  
    50→let activeOps = 0  
    51→const operationQueue: Array<() => void> = []  
    52→  
    53→/**  
    54→ * Acquire a concurrency slot.  
    55→ * Returns a release function that MUST be called in a finally block.  
    56→ * If MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS slots are already taken, queues the caller and  
    57→ * resolves only when a slot becomes available — no busy-waiting, no race.  
    58→ *  
    59→ * The check-and-increment is synchronous (no await between them), so two  
    60→ * concurrent callers cannot both slip through the MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS guard.  
    61→ */  
    62→function acquireSlot(): Promise<() => void> {  
    63→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    64→    const tryAcquire = () => {  
    65→      // Synchronous check-and-increment: no await between them, so this is  
    66→      // the only place activeOps grows and it is always paired with a release.  
    67→      if (activeOps < MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS) {  
    68→        activeOps++  
    69→        resolve(() => {  
    70→          activeOps--  
    71→          // Wake the next queued operation, if any.  
    72→          if (operationQueue.length > 0) {  
    73→            const next = operationQueue.shift()!  
    74→            next()  
    75→          }  
    76→        })  
    77→      } else {  
    78→        operationQueue.push(tryAcquire)  
    79→      }  
    80→    }  
    81→    tryAcquire()  
    82→  })  
    83→}  
    84→  
    85→// In-memory build status tracking (with TTL eviction)  
    86→const buildResults = new Map<string, PluginBuildResult>()  
    87→  
    88→// ============================================================================  
    89→// Validation helpers  
    90→// ============================================================================  
    91→  
    92→const PLUGIN_NAME_RE = /^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*$/  
    93→const GIT_REF_RE = /^[a-zA-Z0-9._\/-]+$/

All changes are correct. The fix is complete.  

**Summary of what was changed in `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-5ec6f8/services/plugin-builder-service.ts`:**  

1. Added `operationQueue` array and `acquireSlot()` function after the `MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS` / `activeOps` declarations. `acquireSlot()` atomically checks-and-increments `activeOps` (synchronous, no `await` between check and increment) and returns a `release` callback. If all slots are full it queues the caller and resolves when a slot is freed.  

2. In `buildPlugin`: replaced `activeOps++` / `activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)` with `const release = await acquireSlot()`, `.finally(release)` on the async `runBuild` chain, and `release()` in the setup-failure catch block.  

3. In `scanRepo`: same replacement — `const release = await acquireSlot()` before the try, `release()` in the finally.  

4. In `pushToGitHub`: same replacement — `const release = await acquireSlot()` before the try, `release()` in the finally.  

[DONE] services/plugin-builder-service.ts - replaced racy check-and-increment activeOps pattern in buildPlugin/scanRepo/pushToGitHub with queue-based acquireSlot() that atomically acquires and releases concurrency slots

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:52:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The findings file doesn't exist but the prompt clearly describes the bug. The single `try/catch` block wraps both `request.json()` and `pushToGitHub()`, so any unexpected error thrown by `pushToGitHub` would be caught and returned as `400 "Invalid request body"` — masking the real error with a wrong status code and misleading message.  

The fix separates them into two try/catch blocks: one around JSON parsing (400) and one around the `pushToGitHub` call (500).  

</div>

```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig

    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Manifest is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)

    if (result.error) {
      // Guard: only use result.status if it is a valid HTTP error code (400-599),
      // otherwise default to 500 to avoid returning a non-error status with an error body.
      const statusCode =
        typeof result.status === 'number' &&
        result.status >= 400 &&
        result.status < 600
          ? result.status
          : 500
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: statusCode }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  // Separate try/catch for JSON parsing so that malformed request bodies
  // return 400, while errors from pushToGitHub return 500.
  let body: PluginPushConfig

    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Fork URL is required' },
      { status: 400 }
    )

   273→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   274→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   275→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   276→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   277→    req.on('end', () => {  
   278→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   279→      if (!body) return resolve({})  
   280→      try {  
   281→        resolve(JSON.parse(body))  
   282→      } catch (e) {  
   283→        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))  
   284→      }  
   285→    })  
   286→    req.on('error', reject)  
   287→  })  
   288→}  
   289→  
   290→async function readRawBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {  
   291→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   292→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   293→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   294→    req.on('end', () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)))  
   295→    req.on('error', reject)  
   296→  })  
   297→}  
   298→  
   299→function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {  
   300→  const body = JSON.stringify(data)  
   301→  res.writeHead(statusCode, {  
   302→    'Content-Type': 'application/json',  
   303→    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),  
   304→    ...headers,  
   305→  })  
   306→  res.end(body)  
   307→}  
   308→  
   309→function sendBinary(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, buffer: Buffer | Uint8Array, headers: Record<string, string>) {  
   310→  res.writeHead(statusCode, headers)  
   311→  res.end(buffer)  
   312→}  
   313→  
   314→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {  
   315→  if (result.error && !result.data) {  
   316→    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)  
   317→  } else {  
   318→    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)  
   319→  }  
   320→}

   209→function getSkillDisplayName(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string {  
   210→  switch (skill.type) {  
   211→    case 'core':  
   212→      return skill.name  
   213→    case 'marketplace':  
   214→      return skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id  
   215→    case 'repo':  
   216→      return skill.name  
   217→  }  
   218→}  
   219→  
   220→function getSkillSubtitle(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string | null {  
   221→  switch (skill.type) {  
   222→    case 'core':  
   223→      return null  
   224→    case 'marketplace':  
   225→      return `${skill.plugin} / ${skill.marketplace}`  
   226→    case 'repo':  
   227→      return skill.url.replace(/^https?:\/\//, '').replace(/\.git$/, '')  
   228→  }

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-5ec6f8/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx`  

**Old:**  
```
    case 'marketplace':
      return skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id
```

**New:**  
```
    case 'marketplace': {
      const parts = skill.id.split(':')
      return parts[parts.length - 1] || skill.id
    }
```

The fix is applied correctly. The block scope (`{}`) was added around the `case 'marketplace'` branch because a `const` declaration inside a `switch` case requires its own block scope — this is both a correctness requirement in TypeScript/JavaScript and prevents the `no-case-declarations` lint error.
